<Rate>3</Rate>< text>
I was looking forward to checking this place out and finally got a chance to stop by here for lunch.
Very nicely designed interior with a bar and outside seating as well. Good choice of beers on tap and a full kitchen.
I ordered what came recommended, which was a sandwich with both turkey and pulled pork as well as a small soup on the side.
Sandwich was quite boring and had more mustard that it needed which, when combined with the pickles resulted in it being too salty and sour with no other taste despite the pulled pork, which according to the staff is cooked in-house. In addition the bread roll was a bit big for the content of the sandwich so I had to remove half of it, which luckily removed some of the mustard as well.
The soup (chicken and rice) was just as dull with no flavor aside from its acidity. The one good thing in it was the red quinoa, which was cooked perfectly and gave it a pleasant, grainy crunch. The white rice was just a cheap filler and did nothing to improve it. I think that a much better soup can be made from grains and veggies with chicken for about the same cost.
I must add that the gentlemen who was serving me was exceptionally polite and helpful and even ran after me to give me the baseball cap I had forgotten.
So maybe this restaurant has better items that I didn't get to try, but in my opinion, if you put something on the menu, you should make it worth tasting. Anyway, I wish them luck.<//text>

< review>
Very cool vibe here. They have a bar, several indoor tables, and an outdoor area as well.

They have a great selection of beers, as well as the basic variety of wines. They appear to specialize in pulled pork and brisket. They also have some chicken and turkey sandwiches, several salads, and a bunch of appetizers.

Most of what we had was pretty good. Prices are fair, and during happy hour there are some real values. Service was good.</review>

< Text>
I was in the area and stopped by for a quick lunch with a pint. There is a cute outdoor patio area and the interior is welcoming and well lit.

I had the BBQ sandwich with pulled pork and a blood orange IPA. The pickled onions were a great touch! (Seeing Alpine Duet on the beer menu is also a bonus.) Staff is very friendly and I didn't wait very long for my food to arrive. Seems like a great place for solo diners, couples, or small groups.< /Text>

<time>1494568831495<//time><Pics>None< /Pics>< Text>
Not a great first impression. We were a party of 8 + a baby. We arrived and it took a while before someone came over and ordered our drinks. I had ordered a coffee and was warned that they would need to brew it so it would be a little wait which was fine. But I had to ask for it 2 more times and finally got it after about 20 minutes. This wasn't too big of a deal and they kindly offered to comp it which was nice. I had the BBQ chicken flatbread which was very good. Honestly the food was all good and we really enjoyed the sauces for the wings. But the service was so slow. We had to wait a while to order drinks, we had to wait a while to order appetizers, we had to wait a while to order entrees, we had to wait a while to order dessert and then had to wait a while to get the check and for them to take the payment. And they weren't very busy at all, so we weren't sure what was going on. Luckily we didn't have a real time crunch, but if you're on a bit of a schedule and have places to go, be prepared to have to keep on the servers to make sure you can get out in a timely manner. We were there for almost 2 and a half hours overall. Again, it wasn't too terrible, but be prepared for bad service.<//Text>

100903848925934605912</user_id>
<name>Kyle Deeley< /name><date>1521395830383< /date>< rate>
4< /rate>
< Review>
Spice & Soul is a neat little restaurant that's off the uber-crowded beaten paths. We found ourselves there after being unable to find parking in Little Italy.

We had wanted pizza, but the pizza place across the street was closed, so Spice & Soul would have to do. We ordered a trio of appetizers: the tri-tip flat bread, the clucks and fries, and the hot mess fries.

The flat bread was fresh and light with a pesto aioli alongside mozzarella serving to cut the heaviness of the tri-tip. The clucks and fries were... Well, they were definitely chicken fingers and fries. Nothing much exciting there, though they were tasty.

The plate that stole the show for me was the hot mess fries. I had wanted it with brisket, but they were out, so I got pork instead. The fries came topped with mountains of meat and cheese. The pork was tender and smoked to perfection. Fantastic!

Spice & Soul gets a 4/5 with me. There was nothing objectionable about their food, but I found it all to lack dimension. I loved the hot mess fries, but it was still missing a little bit of zing or pizzazz to me, and the rest of the food was fine, but not great.

Absolutely check this place out if you're into craft beers, of which there are many, or if you're looking for some great smoked pork. Enjoy!</Review>

< Text>
I've been here a number of times (lunch and dinner, over the past 3 years or so) and have always had a great experience. The decor isn't much to look at, but all of the food I've had has been extremely fresh and well-prepared. The buffet has a good variety, and all of the fresh veggies are beautiful. And you can't beat the price! Added bonus - I've got fairly serious food allergies, and the way they heat the food, it keeps your stuff on a single space on the griddle. I've been to other Mongolian places where they move the food across the whole griddle, so your stuff gets a lot of contamination from other peoples' plates, but here, your food stays on one section of the griddle until it is done.</Text>

I was there today for the 1st time.

It can be hot or not+noddles.They have egg holls or dumplings as appetizers if you prefer you can choose (all ypu can eat or a box.(mixed up all ingredients u choose in one box.

I recomend.</review>

< Text>
This restaurant is surprisingly healthy and tasty!  The way it works is that you get a bowl or two and fill it with veggies, frozen strips of meat and you get a bowl of egg drop soup, rice and bread.  Of course you can go low carb and ditch the rice, bread and noodles and getting only veggies and meat which makes it pretty tasty.  You can buy the all you can eat deal and go back for as many helpings as you'd like.  Part of me is kinda put off because the veggies seem to be canned and the meat is obviously frozen so there's no way to really know the quality of the food you're eating.</Text>

<Rating>5</Rating>< Review>
Skincare Market, Inc. (SMI) is not only a outstanding company, it is an ethical one as well. I placed an order for- 4 KN95 Face Mask 5 Packs on May 21, 2020. The Grand Total for that order was $75.96. On July 29, 2020, another order for KN95 Face Mask 20 Pack was placed. The Grand Total for this order was $36.94. When I asked what was the reason for the price decrease, I was told that SMI found a more competitive supplier for the KN95 Masks and decided to pass any savings to their customers. A practice like I just described is almost unheard of in today's business climate...let alone a business climate challenged by Covid-19! THANK YOU Skincare Market, Inc for always doing a great job but also
DOING THE RIGHT THING!!!!< /Review>
